To do so, we compare the current latest with the *previous* filter. If they\n    35→  // match, then we must be processing a new filter for the first time. We omit this check if we're\n    36→  // the first filter, since the above check handles that case.\n    37→  //\n    38→  // We compare against the previous filter to avoid multiple filter iterations from resetting the\n    39→  // pointer: If we just set latest to current, then the first onData filter iteration would\n    40→  // correctly iterate over the filters and set latest, but on subsequent onData iterations\n    41→  // we'd start from the beginning again, potentially allowing filter N to modify the buffer even\n    42→  // though filter M > N was the filter that inserted data into the buffer.\n    43→  if (current_filter != filters.begin() && latest_filter == std::prev(current_filter)->get()) {\n    44→    latest_filter = current_filter->get();\n    45→  }\n    46→}\n
